What I liked about the sauce and the toppings was that some places that have their own homemade sauce have too much acidity and after about a slice and a half your tongue starts to I feel that acidity. <text>A quick correction to the info on this Google listing: this is NOT part of the "Valentino's" chain of pizza and buffet restaurants in Nebraska, Iowa, Kansas, etc.  They only have two tables for eating inside, and are really geared for take-out or delivery. Pretty basic little place.

Having said that, the folks are friendly and helpful, their take-out window is super busy around dinner time, and I hear they do make pretty good pizza. We just couldn't wait long enough to try it ourselves, and our group wasn't going to fit here anyway... the web link on Google made us think they had plenty of seating! Oops.

So for the record, their link to the website for the Midwest chain is not correct. As of this review, this restaurant doesn't have its own website.<//text>< pics>

< Review>
I stumbled upon Monkey Face Tattoos & shop owner Baron Davis by accident after deciding to have a sleeve worked on. Upon meeting Baron, I noticed a clean and welcoming lounge area-- complete with some unobstructive music and television on to help with a really relaxed and easygoing environment. Clearly on display is some of his portfolios on display for review in order to showcase his legitimacy and achievements throughout his professional career. While talking to Baron, he acted as a consultant, not a salesperson and really understood what it is I was looking for with an extensive tattoo job. Understanding what it is I was looking for, he took his time and carefully drew a piece reflective of what I was looking for which was a reflection of my heritage. Additionally, rather than rush the extensive job, he broke up the job in several segments over the course of many months. The bottom line is that while he's not cheap in the least bit, the quality of the tattoo job has been second to none, especially in the part of Los Angeles he is based in where tattoo shops are fairly uncommon. Easily one of the best in the city and HIGHLY recommended.<//Review>

< Review>
I was road tripping through the area and saw this place had a bunch of good reviews and a pretty stellar rating. It was a ghost town when I showed up, which for the time of day didnt seem too strange. the place was clean and the woman working that morning greeted us promptly. We got water to start and took a sec to look through the menu, nothing special, just your standard mexican restaurant fare. The woman brought out chips and pico, to start and the chips were horribly over cooked and came in odd shapes that made dipping very difficult as well as having a sort of stale taste to begin with. I ordered the special carnitas nachos with jalepenos added to them and a few chorizo street tacos, my companion ordered a bean and cheese burrito. Let the dissapointment begin...
There were no tantalizing smells of food getting prepared in the kitchen, no clanking of pans or sounds of fresh sausage sizzling, just the unashamed open and close of a microwave door while the woman sat in a stool by the front. When I received my nachos, I couldnt fricken believe it, the cheese sauce looked like yellow baby vommit separating from itself and watery, the carnitas were hard looking and a strange hue of greenish brown with this irridescense to the surface, and she had put whole pickled jalepenos and carrots over the top of them just coating my stale old nightmare nachos in vinegar. The presentation was bad, the taste was horrific and it wasnt even luke warm. After that got to the table I decided it was time to go. I couldnt imagine what the other food would be like if the nachos were ruined so badly. And like I guessed not even the chorizo deserved to be cooked fresh in her mind, she started bringing what looked like poorly cooked(in the first place whenever that was) leftovers and we got the hell outta there, I was shocked and taken by surprise that an establishment could be so terrible, so lifeless that the food would be that way, I felt bad, because she must be on here way out of the biz so I paid but it was almost 40 dollars for the aforementioned slop plus 1 beer and a bottled coke. Just crazy, never again! Dont send your friends or your enemies to Ricardas. Id have rather been punched in the face and saved my 40 bucks than to have burnt it in that dumpster.<//Review>

<user>110974608296923840794<//user><Name>Nicole Gir√≥n<//Name>< Date>
1503851439364</Date>
<rate>1< /rate>< Review>
Being a Southern Californian latina, and growing up with extensive knowledge with Mexican and Latino foods. I have to say that I'm very disappointed in the pricing and the quality of food that was given to me at Ricardas.
Menudo is $11.00 when it should be $8.00, (it's just broth and tri-tip) flavorless, and you can absolutely tell that it was sitting in a cauldron all day. It was luke-warm when it came to my table. Did not finish it.

The Carn√© Asada was old, bland and didn't have that fresh off the grill taste or feeling that asada is suppose to have.
I feel like the woman taking my order was taking advantage of the English speakers in her restaurant. Trying to upsale at every moment.

It makes me sad to see Mexican Americans loose pride and dignity in their cultural dishes, just because we are a consumerist country. The employees of Ricardas know that they are a minority in town and any dish will sell.

Don't waste your time here, way better places to eat in Bragg.
Im still dealing with a stomach ache from just soup and two tacos.</Review>

< Review>
There was ample parking for the mass we attended, though it did not seem like there would be when we arrived. The music was easy enough to follow along though the style wasn't my favorite as I'm more of a traditionalist. There was a diverse crowd of worshipers and the dress code was more 'come as you are' than 'Sunday best'. Parishioners were friendly. There were a lot of families with children, kids who weren't into the mass, and the usual kid noise.</Review>

I don't really like this school. There is no art programs, snobby rich kids, and no usage of computer technology. People in the work office are using computers more than ever,and I don't want my classmates to fall behind. If I was in charge of this school,I would bring back the computer room and add drawing tablets.
Another thing about this school that annoys me is how cheap it is. They can't hire chefs to cook for the antique show,so they have to use the Lady's Guild instead. I mean if they get 7,000 dollars from each parent,that should be enough money to buy stuff. Think about it like this,if there are 600 kids in St.Chris and each one of their parents gives 7,000  dollars it would be 4,200,000 dollars total. < review>
Scripps Coastal Reserve occupies nearly one thousand acres in La Jolla, California, ranging across a complex landscape including mesa top, coastal canyon and bluff, sandy beach, rocky intertidal, submerged coastal plain and deep submarine canyon. Hundreds of thousands of people visit annually, so environmental awareness is essential for protecting the rare and sensitive habitats and species. There are two distinct parts to the reserve: the shoreline and marine protected area, and the upland area, commonly referred to as the ‚ÄúKnoll‚Äù or ‚ÄúCliffs.‚Äù The Reserve is a great landscape to explore and visit whilst on your journey.<//review>
